- Objects:

 Here are the detailed transformation steps for converting the input grid into the output grid:

1. Identify all objects of color 3 located at the rightmost part of the grid with a size greater than 1. To do this, iterate through each object in the input grid and check if its color is 3, it is located at the rightmost part of the grid (i.e., the last column), and its size is greater than 1. Add these objects to a list of objects to be shifted.

For example, in Example\_1, Object\_3, Object\_5, Object\_10, and Object\_12 are added to the list of objects to be shifted. Similarly, in Example\_2, Object\_4, Object\_8, and Object\_14 are added to the list. In Example\_3, no objects are added to the list since there are no objects of color 3 located at the rightmost part of the grid with a size greater than 1.

2. Determine the distance to shift each object. This distance can be any positive integer value less than the size of the object. For simplicity, we can choose the distance to be half of the size of the object, rounded down.

For example, in Example\_1, Object\_3 has a size of 2, so we shift it by 1 unit to the left. Object\_5 has a size of 4, so we shift it by 2 units to the left. Similarly, Object\_10 is shifted by 2 units to the left, and Object\_12 is shifted by 1 unit to the left. In Example\_2, Object\_4 is shifted by 1 unit to the left, Object\_8 is shifted by 2 units to the left, and Object\_14 is shifted by 1 unit to the left.

3. Update the coordinates of each object in the list of objects to be shifted. For each object, subtract the distance determined in step 2 from the x-coordinate of each point in the object's coordinate list.

For example, in Example\_1, after shifting Object\_3 by 1 unit to the left, its new coordinate list becomes [[3, 3], [4, 3]]. Similarly, Object\_5 is updated to [[1, 4], [2, 4], [3, 4], [4, 4]], Object\_10 is updated to [[4, 7], [5, 7], [6, 7], [7, 7]], and Object\_12 is updated to [[0, 8]]. In Example\_2, Object\_4 is updated to [[5, 1], [6, 1], [7, 1]], Object\_8 is updated to [[2, 4], [3, 4], [4, 4], [5, 4]], and Object\_14 is updated to [[0, 8]].

4. Create the output grid by replacing the objects in the input grid with the updated objects from the list of objects to be shifted.

Sample Outputs:
 Here are the detailed transformation steps for converting the input grid into the output grid:

1. Initialize an empty output grid with the same dimensions as the input grid.
2. For each object in the input grid, perform the following steps:
   a. Check if the object has another object with a larger size above it. If yes, adjust the object's y-coordinate (i.e., row index) by adding one to its current value until it reaches an empty space or a smaller object.
   b. Check if the adjusted object is still within the bounds of the grid. If it is outside the grid, leave it as is and move on to the next object. Otherwise, update the corresponding cells in the output grid with the object's color value.
3. Repeat step 2 for all objects in the input grid.
4. Return the output grid.
